{{very long|date=August 2020}}
{{Windows 10}}
<section begin=Lede /><!-- needed for transcluding into other pages if this page needs to be split-->[[Windows 10]] is an [[operating system]] developed by [[Microsoft]]. Microsoft described Windows 10 as an "[[software as a service|operating system as a service]]" that would receive ongoing updates to its features and functionality, augmented with the ability for enterprise environments to receive non-critical updates at a slower pace or use long-term support milestones that will only receive critical updates, such as security patches, over their five-year lifespan of mainstream support.<section end=Lede />

== Channels ==
{{Main|Windows Insider#Channels}}
{{Windows 10 versions}}
[[Windows Insider|Windows 10 Insider]] Preview builds are delivered to Insiders in three different channels (previously "rings").<ref name=BlogsByWindowsonRings>{{cite news|last=Aul|first=Gabe|title=We're rolling out our first new build to the Windows Insider Program|url=http://blogs.windows.com/bloggingwindows/2014/10/21/were-rolling-out-our-first-new-build-to-the-windows-insider-program|newspaper=Windows Blog|date=October 21, 2014}}</ref> Insiders in the Dev Channel (previously ''Fast Ring'') receive updates prior to those in then Beta Channel (previously ''Slow Ring''), but might experience more bugs and other issues.<ref name=WMPowerUserSR>{{cite news|last=Hassan|first=Mehedi|title=[WP10] Microsoft releases Slow ring for Windows 10 for Phones Technical Preview|url=http://wmpoweruser.com/wp10-microsoft-releases-slow-ring-windows-10-phones-technical-preview|newspaper=Windows Mobile PowerUser|date=February 19, 2015}}</ref><ref name=WMPowerUserDVRT>{{cite news|last=Hassan|first=Mehedi|title=Video Recorder on Windows 10 for Phones Preview introduces couple of new features|url=http://wmpoweruser.com/video-recorder-windows-10-phones-preview-slow-ring-introduces-couple-new-features|newspaper=Windows Mobile PowerUser|date=February 19, 2015}}</ref> Insiders in the Release Preview Channel (previously ''Release Preview Ring'') do not receive updates until the version is almost available to the public, but are comparatively more stable.<ref name=windowscentral>{{cite news|last=Rubino|first=Daniel|title=Which Windows Insider Ring is best? All you need to know about Slow, Fast, and Release Preview rings|url=http://windowscentral.com/all-you-need-know-about-windows-insider-rings|newspaper=Windows Central|date=May 6, 2016}}</ref>
{{Clear}}

== PC version history ==
Mainstream builds of Windows 10 are labeled "YYMM", with YY representing the two-digit year and MM representing the month of planned release (for example, version 1507 refers to builds which initially released in July 2015). 

{|class="wikitable"
|-float=center
!Legend:
|{{legend2|#fdb3ab|{{abbr|Old version|Windows 10 builds that have this color have reached their expiration dates and are no longer supported by Microsoft.}}|border=1px solid #AAAAAA}}
|{{legend2|#fef8c6|{{abbr|Older version, still maintained|Windows 10 builds that have this color are no longer the latest version of Windows 10, but are still supported by Microsoft.}}|border=1px solid #AAAAAA}}
|{{legend2|#d4f4b4|{{abbr|'''Latest version'''|Windows 10 builds that have this color are the latest public version of Windows 10.}}|border=1px solid #AAAAAA}}
|{{legend2|#c1e6f5|{{abbr|Preview version|Windows 10 builds that have this color are Insider Preview builds, and are not the latest public version.}}|border=1px solid #AAAAAA}}
|}

=== Version 1507 ===
The original version of Windows 10 (also [[Retronym|retroactively named]] '''version 1507''' and codenamed  '''"Threshold 1"''') was released in July 2015. It carries the build number 10.0.10240; while Microsoft has stated that there was no designated [[release to manufacturing]] (RTM) build of Windows 10, build 10240 was described as an RTM build by various media outlets.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://extremetech.com/computing/210787-windows-10-build-10240-is-the-rtm-version-but-microsoft-wishes-youd-stop-calling-it-that|title=Windows 10 Build 10240 is the RTM version, but Microsoft wishes you’d stop calling it that – ExtremeTech|work=ExtremeTech|accessdate=August 4, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150804012250/http://www.extremetech.com/computing/210787-windows-10-build-10240-is-the-rtm-version-but-microsoft-wishes-youd-stop-calling-it-that|archive-date=August 4, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://news.softpedia.com/news/windows-10-has-reached-rtm-487002.shtml|title=Windows 10 Has Reached RTM|first=Bogdan|last=Popa|date=July 15, 2015|work=softpedia|accessdate=August 4, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150724183111/http://news.softpedia.com/news/windows-10-has-reached-rtm-487002.shtml|archive-date=July 24, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://winbeta.org/news/its-official-windows-10-has-reached-rtm|title=Windows 10 hits RTM milestone ahead of July 29th launch|work=WinBeta|accessdate=August 4, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150910191817/http://www.winbeta.org/news/its-official-windows-10-has-reached-rtm|archive-date=September 10, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=verge-numbermeaning>{{cite web|title=Windows 10's final build number is delightfully clever|url=https://theverge.com/2015/7/15/8945373/windows-10-rtm-final-build-number|website=The Verge|accessdate=July 27, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150728071837/http://www.theverge.com/2015/7/15/8945373/windows-10-rtm-final-build-number|archive-date=July 28, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=thurrott-notrtm>{{cite web|last1=Thurrott|first1=Paul|title=No RTM for Windows 10, Microsoft Says|url=https://thurrott.com/windows/windows-10/4797/no-rtm-for-windows-10-microsoft-says|website=Thurrott.com|accessdate=July 27, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150723121552/https://www.thurrott.com/windows/windows-10/4797/no-rtm-for-windows-10-microsoft-says|archive-date=July 23, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=verge-rtmfinalized>{{cite web|title=Microsoft has finalized Windows 10|url=https://theverge.com/2015/7/15/8950481/microsoft-windows-10-rtm-date|website=The Verge|publisher=Vox Media|accessdate=July 15, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150715172408/http://www.theverge.com/2015/7/15/8950481/microsoft-windows-10-rtm-date|archive-date=July 15, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> It was retroactively named "version 1507" by Microsoft per its naming conventions for future stable releases of the operating system.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/release-info.aspx?f=255&MSPPError=-2147217396|title=Windows 10 release information – current branch, build history|website=technet.microsoft.com|accessdate=March 7, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160308064257/https://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/release-info.aspx?f=255&MSPPError=-2147217396|archive-date=March 8, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref>

Notable changes in this version include:<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.laptopmag.com/articles/windows-10-top-features|title=Top 10 New Windows 10 Features|last1=Low|first1=Cherlynn|date=January 21, 2014|website=Laptop Mag|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190416031109/https://www.laptopmag.com/articles/windows-10-top-features|archive-date=April 16, 2019|url-status=live|accessdate=May 7, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theverge.com/2015/7/29/9060177/microsoft-windows-10-update-changes-browser-start-menu-cortana-xbox|title=The nine most important updates in Windows 10|last1=Seifert|first1=Dan|date=July 29, 2015|website=[[The Verge]]|publisher=Vox Media, Inc.|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190428210646/https://www.theverge.com/2015/7/29/9060177/microsoft-windows-10-update-changes-browser-start-menu-cortana-xbox|archive-date=April 28, 2019|url-status=live|access-date=May 7, 2019}}</ref>
* An updated [[start menu]]
* The introduction of [[Cortana]], a virtual assistant, to the desktop version of Windows
* A "Continuum" mode that allows users to switch between desktop mode and tablet mode
* "Action Center", which includes notifications and quick access to settings
* A new web browser, [[Microsoft Edge]], that replaces [[Internet Explorer]] as the default browser in Windows
* Improved multitasking, including virtual desktops
* Many updated built-in apps

The final release was made available to Windows Insiders on July 15, 2015, followed by a public release on July 29, 2015. Support of version 1507 ended on May 9, 2017 for devices in the Current Branch and Current Branch for Business; however, devices configured to receive updates from the Current Branch and Current Branch for Business continued to receive updates until June 27, 2018.<ref name="ms-win10-release-info">{{cite web|url=https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/release-information/|title=Windows 10 release information|last=|first=|date=|website=Microsoft Docs|publisher=[[Microsoft]]|language=en-us|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190507061309/https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/release-information/|archive-date=May 7, 2019|url-status=live|access-date=May 7, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 version 1507 on CB and CBB are still receiving updates|url=https://twitter.com/ChangeWindows/status/875801158526406656|accessdate=June 19, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190218100055/https://twitter.com/ChangeWindows/status/875801158526406656|archive-date=February 18, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>

| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|6.4.9841<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://neowin.net/news/download-windows-10-technical-preview|title=Download: Windows 10 Technical Preview|date=December 1, 2014|work=Neowin|publisher=Neowin|accessdate=November 6, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161107093155/https://www.neowin.net/news/download-windows-10-technical-preview|archive-date=November 7, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/10/01/join-the-windows-insider-program-and-get-the-windows-10-technical-preview/#pRkTscRi4lT2RBep.97|title=Join the Windows Insider Program and get the Windows 10 Technical Preview|date=October 1, 2014|newspaper=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=November 6, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161107092713/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/10/01/join-the-windows-insider-program-and-get-the-windows-10-technical-preview/#pRkTscRi4lT2RBep.97|archive-date=November 7, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref>
|October 1, 2014
|
This is the first public preview build of Microsoft Windows 10. It introduces a hybrid start menu that combines the functionality of that of Windows 7 and Windows 8.1. In this build, "Metro-Style" apps, direct predecessors to UWP apps, can be run in floating windows. Improvements are made to window management with the introduction of Task View that features virtual desktops. Other improvements in this area include the expansion of the window snapping feature allowing apps to be snapped on up to four corners with "Snap Assist" feature that suggest other windows to snap when the users snaps a window.<ref name="b9841">{{cite web|url=https://theverge.com/2014/9/30/6868695/microsoft-windows-10-announced-official|title=Windows 10 is the official name for Microsoft's next version of Windows|last=Warren|first=Tom|date=September 30, 2014|website=The Verge|accessdate=November 7, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161221112700/http://www.theverge.com/2014/9/30/6868695/microsoft-windows-10-announced-official|archive-date=December 21, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10|last=Aul|first=Gabe|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/09/30/announcing-windows-10|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=[[Microsoft]]|accessdate=November 22, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151004172931/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/09/30/announcing-windows-10/|archive-date=October 4, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>

The Windows command line console is updated with this build with new functionalities including, allowing users to cut, copy, and paste texts with the standard keyboard shortcuts, the ability to display the console at full screen at any display resolution, and transparency options.{{r|b9841}}<ref>{{cite news|url=https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2014/09/windows-10-command-prompt-finally-gets-dragged-into-the-21st-century|title=Windows 10 command prompt finally gets dragged into the 21st century|newspaper=Ars Technica|accessdate=November 7, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161029042215/http://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2014/09/windows-10-command-prompt-finally-gets-dragged-into-the-21st-century/|archive-date=October 29, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref>
|-valign="top"
| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|6.4.9860<br /><ref>{{cite news|url=https://neowin.net/news/windows-10-technical-preview-build-9860-is-out-download-it-now|title=Windows 10 Technical Preview build 9860 is out, download it now|newspaper=Neowin|accessdate=November 6, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161107093113/https://www.neowin.net/news/windows-10-technical-preview-build-9860-is-out-download-it-now|archive-date=November 7, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://makeuseof.com/tag/priority-windows-10-tp-build-9860|title=Windows 10 Is Evolving – This Is What's New In Build 9860|newspaper=MakeUseOf|accessdate=November 6, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161107155446/http://www.makeuseof.com/tag/priority-windows-10-tp-build-9860/|archive-date=November 7, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref>
|October 21, 2014
|
The second public preview build of Windows 10 introduces Action Center, which debuted in Windows Phone 8.1.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/10/21/were-rolling-out-our-first-new-build-to-the-windows-insider-program|title=We're rolling out our first new build to the Windows Insider Program|last1=Aul|first1=Gabe|date=October 21, 2014|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=February 14, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151006152952/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/10/21/were-rolling-out-our-first-new-build-to-the-windows-insider-program/|archive-date=October 6, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>
|-valign="top"
| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|6.4.9879<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/11/12/new-build-available-to-the-windows-insider-program|title=New build available to the Windows Insider Program|last1=Gabe|first1=Aul|date=November 12, 2014|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=February 14, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151005011619/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/11/12/new-build-available-to-the-windows-insider-program/|archive-date=October 5, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>
|'''Fast ring:'''<br />November 12, 2014<br />'''Slow ring:'''<br />November 25, 2014
|
This is the last public preview build to have the version number of 6.4. This build brought upon one of the most controversial changes to the operating system by removing the [[OneDrive]]'s "Smart Files" that allowed users to view and work with files on OneDrive through File Explorer even if they were not synced to the device. OneDrive now uses selective synchronization of local contents with the cloud service.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://mspoweruser.com/microsoft-responds-to-onedrive-changes-in-windows-10-build-9879-smart-files-are-not-coming-back|title=Microsoft Responds To OneDrive Changes In Windows 10 Build 9879, Smart Files Are Not Coming Back|last=Pradeep|date=November 15, 2014|work=MSPowerUser|publisher=MSPowerUser|accessdate=February 14, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161107221515/https://mspoweruser.com/microsoft-responds-to-onedrive-changes-in-windows-10-build-9879-smart-files-are-not-coming-back/|archive-date=November 7, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="b9879">{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/11/12/new-build-available-to-the-windows-insider-program|title=New build available to the Windows Insider Program|last=Aul|first=Gabe|date=November 12, 2014|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=[[Microsoft]]|accessdate=November 23, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151005011619/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2014/11/12/new-build-available-to-the-windows-insider-program/|archive-date=October 5, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>

Other UI changes in this build include the ability to hide the "Task View" and "Search" buttons from the Taskbar, updated minimize and restore animations, updated menu icon for "Metro-Style" apps from 3 dots to [[hamburger button|hamburger-style icon]].{{r|b9879}}

New 3 finger gestures have also been added to switch to Task View and switch between virtual desktops.{{r|b9879}}

[[Internet Explorer]] contains opt-in preview of new [[EdgeHTML]] rendering engine.<ref name=ieblog-spartan>{{cite web|title=Project Spartan and the Windows 10 January Preview Build|url=http://blogs.msdn.com/b/ie/archive/2015/01/22/project-spartan-and-the-windows-10-january-preview-build.aspx|website=IEBlog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=January 23, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150122231219/http://blogs.msdn.com/b/ie/archive/2015/01/22/project-spartan-and-the-windows-10-january-preview-build.aspx|archive-date=January 22, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Living on the Edge – our next step in helping the web just work|url=http://blogs.msdn.com/b/ie/archive/2014/11/11/living-on-the-edge-our-next-step-in-interoperability.aspx|website=IEBlog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=January 23, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150111145128/http://blogs.msdn.com/b/ie/archive/2014/11/11/living-on-the-edge-our-next-step-in-interoperability.aspx|archive-date=January 11, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=verge-spartanannounce>{{cite web|title=Microsoft officially announces Project Spartan, its new web browser for Windows 10|url=https://theverge.com/2015/1/21/7863331/microsoft-project-spartan-new-web-browser|website=The Verge|accessdate=January 21, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150121193927/http://www.theverge.com/2015/1/21/7863331/microsoft-project-spartan-new-web-browser|archive-date=January 21, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>

This build brings native support for [[Matroska]] file types. It also brings [[Windows 10#Operating system compression|Operating system compression]] through the Disk Cleanup utility.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://zdnet.com/pictures/hands-on-with-windows-10-preview-build-9879/3|title=Hands-on with Windows 10 Preview build 9879|last1=Bott|first1=Ed|date=November 13, 2014|website=ZDNet|publisher=CBS Interactive|accessdate=March 17, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150320063441/http://www.zdnet.com/pictures/hands-on-with-windows-10-preview-build-9879/3/|archive-date=March 20, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>
|-valign="top"
| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|10.0.9926<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/01/23/january-build-now-available-to-the-windows-insider-program|title=January build now available to the Windows Insider Program|last1=Aul|first1=Gabe|date=January 23, 2015|website=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=February 14, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151003011253/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/01/23/january-build-now-available-to-the-windows-insider-program/|archive-date=October 3, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>
|'''Fast and slow ring:'''<br />January 23, 2015
|
This build was released after Microsoft's January Windows 10 event where it showed off its upcoming roadmap for the operating system as well as introduced new hardware, including the [[Hololens]] and [[Surface Hub]]. This build brings an all-new Start menu built on top of the UWP APIs. It replaces the Start menu and Start screen, built on legacy [[DirectUI]] used on Previous Windows builds and releases. A full screen button is added to the new Start menu, allowing the user to toggle the full-screen experience without having to go to the Settings app, logging out, and logging back in, as it was required in previous builds.<ref>{{cite web|title=Windows 10: a closer look at the future of Microsoft's vision for PCs|url=https://theverge.com/2015/1/28/7927109/windows-10-features-hands-on|website=The Verge|publisher=Vox Media|accessdate=February 7, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150208001246/http://www.theverge.com/2015/1/28/7927109/windows-10-features-hands-on|archive-date=February 8, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>

This build is the first build to introduce [[UWP apps|Universal Windows Platform (UWP) apps]]. It introduces the beta version of the Windows Store built using the UWP APIs. It also debuts the new Xbox app, which Microsoft announced would be used to stream Xbox One games directly to the PC.<ref name=engadget-w10xbox>{{cite web|title=Xbox on Windows 10: social features, game DVR and more|url=https://engadget.com/2015/01/21/microsoft-windows-10-xbox|website=Engadget|publisher=AOL|accessdate=January 21, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150122003137/http://www.engadget.com/2015/01/21/microsoft-windows-10-xbox/|archive-date=January 22, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> A new alarm app is featured and it includes a world clock, timer, and stop watch<ref>[https://twitter.com/GabeAul/status/562745376328130561 Gabriel Aul on Twitter: "@LuigiLaera We'll be bringing the Windows10 Alarms app to phones. As a Windows App, the same code will run on both platforms."] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160308094728/https://twitter.com/gabeaul/status/562745376328130561 |date=2016-03-08 }}. Twitter.com (February 3, 2015). Retrieved on February 9, 2015.</ref> A new UWP [[Calculator (Windows)|Calculator]] app replaces the traditional Win32 calculator. [[Bing Maps|Maps]] app with Cortana integration<ref>{{cite web|url=http://news.microsoft.com/windows10story|title=Microsoft Windows 10 Event January 2015 (Full)|date=January 21, 2015|publisher=Microsoft|access-date=February 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200109195152/https://news.microsoft.com/windows10story/|archive-date=January 9, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> and ability to save maps for offline use<ref name=neowinofflinemaps>{{cite web|last1=Sams|first1=Brad|title=Windows 10: Offline maps arrive on the desktop with build 9888|url=http://neowin.net/news/windows-10-offline-maps-arrive-on-the-desktop-with-build-9888|website=Neowin|accessdate=April 4, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150630154457/http://www.neowin.net/news/windows-10-offline-maps-arrive-on-the-desktop-with-build-9888|archive-date=June 30, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> A new Photos app is introduced with aggregated content and automatic enhancements.<ref name=verge-thisiswp10>{{cite web|title=This is Windows 10 for phones|url=https://theverge.com/2015/1/21/7869441/windows-10-for-phones-features-hands-on|website=The Verge|publisher=Vox Media|accessdate=January 22, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150122020836/http://www.theverge.com/2015/1/21/7869441/windows-10-for-phones-features-hands-on|archive-date=January 22, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>

[[Cortana (software)|Cortana]] is introduced on the PC for the first time, with support for [[American English|U.S. English]] locale.

There are other user interface changes with this build, including restyled window frames and support for new languages. The Settings app is updated with new layout<ref name=cnet-settingsmenu>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 Settings Menu: The System tab|url=https://cnet.com/how-to/windows-10-settings-menu-the-system-tab|website=CNET|accessdate=February 7, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150208010206/http://www.cnet.com/how-to/windows-10-settings-menu-the-system-tab/|archive-date=February 8, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> The Taskbar is restyled with new opaque appearance, smaller application icons, and underlines to denote active applications. The Action Center is redesigned and includes with quick action buttons.<ref name=pcpro-settingsmenu>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 review: Technical Preview (January 2015)|url=http://alphr.com/microsoft/microsoft-windows-10/25290/windows-10-uk-release-everything-you-need-to-know|website=PC Pro|accessdate=February 7, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150803071634/http://www.alphr.com/microsoft/microsoft-windows-10/25290/windows-10-uk-release-everything-you-need-to-know|archive-date=August 3, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> The search button on the Taskbar is changed to a search box by default. Option to pick default folder when opening [[File Explorer]] is added with this build. Early version of [[DirectX]] 12 is also included.
|-valign="top"
| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|10.0.10041<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/03/18/windows-10-technical-preview-build-10041-now-available|title=Windows 10 Technical Preview Build 10041 now available|first1=Gabe|last1=Aul|date=March 18, 2015|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=March 18, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151005011624/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/03/18/windows-10-technical-preview-build-10041-now-available/|archive-date=October 5, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>
|'''Fast ring:'''<br />March 18, 2015
'''Slow ring:'''<br />March 24, 2015
|
This build brings Cortana support to China, France, Germany, Italy, Spain, and United Kingdom. App updates for this build include Insider Hub, Photos, and Windows Feedback. User Interface changes include the addition of network connections fly-out that can be invoked from the taskbar, handwriting input canvas optimizations for short text entries, lock screen changes with "did you know" backgrounds to help users with Windows 10. The Start button is smaller and has a new hover animation. Functional changes and the addition of transparency to the Start menu. Open applications no longer appear on the taskbar across all virtual desktops by default and can be moved across desktops.

This build also adds the ability to unlock devices with Windows Hello, but requires manufacturers to implement a camera with said capabilities. Print to [[Portable Document Format|PDFs]] is also added.

Bio Enrollment is also added, although its purpose is still not known and the app is not accessible.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://windowscentral.com/microsoft-bundles-bio-enrollment-app-latest-windows-10-tech-preview-build|title=Latest Windows 10 build bundles mysterious Bio Enrollment app|last=|first=|date=|work=|accessdate=|via=|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050357/https://www.windowscentral.com/microsoft-bundles-bio-enrollment-app-latest-windows-10-tech-preview-build|archive-date=2019-10-31|url-status=live}}</ref>

| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|10.0.10061<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/04/22/windows-10-technical-preview-build-10061-now-available|title=Windows 10 Technical Preview Build 10061 now available|first1=Gabe|last1=Aul|date=April 22, 2015|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=April 22, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151005221941/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/04/22/windows-10-technical-preview-build-10061-now-available/|archive-date=October 5, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://venturebeat.com/2015/04/22/microsoft-pushes-out-windows-10-preview-with-new-mail-and-calendar-apps-unlimited-virtual-desktops-bug-fixes|title=Microsoft pushes out Windows 10 preview with new mail and calendar apps, tablet optimization|work=VentureBeat|date=April 22, 2015|first=Mark|last=Sullivan|access-date=February 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050329/https://venturebeat.com/2015/04/22/microsoft-pushes-out-windows-10-preview-with-new-mail-and-calendar-apps-unlimited-virtual-desktops-bug-fixes/|archive-date=October 31, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://theverge.com/2015/4/22/8471547/windows-10-preview-outlook-mail-calendar-apps|title=Windows 10 preview now includes new Outlook mail app and theme tweaks|work=The Verge|date=April 22, 2015|first=Tom|last=Warren|access-date=February 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050345/https://www.theverge.com/2015/4/22/8471547/windows-10-preview-outlook-mail-calendar-apps|archive-date=October 31, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>
|'''Fast ring:'''<br />April 22, 2015
|
This build features several new apps as well as improvements to existing UWP apps. The [[Mail (Windows)|Mail]], Calendar, [[MSN Weather]], [[MSN Money]], and other apps have been updated with new interfaces and improved performance. Preview versions of the Music and Video apps are included along with their Windows 8 counterparts. Microsoft Solitaire Collection is now included with the operating system.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://businessinsider.com/microsoft-solitaire-returning-to-windows-10-2015-4|title=Microsoft is bringing back Solitaire for Windows 10|accessdate=April 30, 2015|author=Tweedie, Steven|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150427000309/http://www.businessinsider.com/microsoft-solitaire-returning-to-windows-10-2015-4|archive-date=April 27, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref>

This build also brings several UI changes. There is now a new black system theme across the Start menu, Taskbar and Action Center. There is now transparency in the Start menu, the Taskbar, the Action Center, and preview windows, with options to enable or disable it. The Start menu is now resizable. Visuals have been refined for desktop icons, close buttons, and thumbnails.

Tablet mode is improved such that entering Tablet mode now causes the Start button, Cortana, and the Task View buttons to all grow in size and space out to be more touch friendly. There is also a new setting to boot direct into Tablet Mode. For tablets under 10 inches, this is the default behavior.

Microsoft Edge has received improvement such that double-clicking on its titlebar now maximizes the application.

|'''Fast and slow ring:'''<br />April 29, 2015
|
Released alongside Microsoft's 2015 build conference, this build introduces new default Windows system sounds. Cortana's user interface is significantly improved; it is now more seamlessly integrated with the Start Menu. Enhancements are made to live tiles, including new animations and the addition the option to disable a live tile. The Start menu's UI has been further refined. Through A/B testing, select users are chosen to experience a translucent Start menu with background blur. The settings app has been improved, including the addition of desktop personalization within the app.

|'''Fast ring:'''<br />May 20, 2015
|
Changes to the desktop user interface is included with this build. The File Explorer and Settings icons in the Start menu are moved to the bottom, near the Power option. The ability to toggle between Start menu and Start screen was moved to the new Start settings page under Personalization settings. People, MSN Weather, MSN Money, Insider Hub, and other apps have been updated with new interfaces and improved performance Microsoft Edge received a New Tab page.

This build also brings changes to how Windows 10 handles default apps. Now, apps cannot modify default apps;only the end user can do so from the Settings app. If an app attempts to change the defaults, the user will simply receive a message describing how to manually change the default apps.
|-valign="top"
| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|10.0.10130<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/05/29/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-10130-for-pcs|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 10130 for PCs|first1=Gabe|last1=Aul|date=May 29, 2015|work=Windows Experience Blog|publisher=Microsoft|accessdate=May 29, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151007051548/http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/05/29/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-10130-for-pcs/|archive-date=October 7, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://pcworld.com/article/2928206/windows-10-build-10130-adds-cortana-button-new-icons-start-improvements.html|title=Windows 10 Build 10130 adds Cortana button, new icons, Start improvements|work=[[PC World]]|date=May 29, 2015|first=Mark|last=Hachman|access-date=February 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180526045828/https://www.pcworld.com/article/2928206/windows-10-build-10130-adds-cortana-button-new-icons-start-improvements.html|archive-date=May 26, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref>

This build brings various visual improvements. Users can now customize Start experience by opening the Settings app > Personalization > Start. There are new icon throughout the operating system. Jump Lists on the taskbar and Start menu, first introduced in Windows 7, are rebuilt using UWP APIs. Further improvements are made to tablet mode, video playback with the [[Microsoft Movies & TV|Movies & TV]] app, and Microsoft Edge (still named Project Spartan in this build). This build also adds the ability to print to PDF natively.

Starting with this build, Cortana's speech recognition can be launched using {{key press|[[Windows Key|Win]]|[[C]]}}.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://slashgear.com/windows-10-preview-build-10130-cortana-shortcut-and-more-29385976|title=Windows 10 preview build 10130: Cortana shortcut and more|last=Roston|first=Brittany A.|date=May 29, 2015|work=SlashGear|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150530230152/http://www.slashgear.com/windows-10-preview-build-10130-cortana-shortcut-and-more-29385976/|archive-date=May 30, 2015|url-status=dead|access-date=May 7, 2019}}</ref>

| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|10.0.10158<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/06/29/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-10158-for-pcs|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 10158 for PCs|work=windows.com|access-date=2020-02-07|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050415/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2015/06/29/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-10158-for-pcs/|archive-date=2019-10-31|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://betanews.com/2015/06/29/windows-10-build-10158-for-pc-featuring-dark-theme-laced-microsoft-edge-cooler-cortana-available-to-download|title=Windows 10 Build 10158 for PC featuring dark theme-laced Microsoft Edge, cooler Cortana available to download|work=Beta News|date=June 30, 2015|first=Manish|last=Singh|access-date=February 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050340/https://betanews.com/2015/06/29/windows-10-build-10158-for-pc-featuring-dark-theme-laced-microsoft-edge-cooler-cortana-available-to-download/|archive-date=October 31, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://zdnet.com/article/microsofts-latest-windows-10-preview-for-pcs-gets-edge-browser-branding|title=Microsoft's latest Windows 10 preview for PCs gets Edge browser branding|work=[[ZDNet]] (All About Microsoft)|date=June 30, 2015|first=Mary Jo|last=Foley|access-date=February 7, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160629235335/http://www.zdnet.com/article/microsofts-latest-windows-10-preview-for-pcs-gets-edge-browser-branding/|archive-date=June 29, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref>
|'''Fast ring:'''<br />June 29, 2015
|
This build brings further UX improvements and refinements, updates to Cortana and its integration with apps and services. This build also includes app updates, including updates to the photos app and the Snipping Tool app that allows the capture of screenshot after a user defined timer. Starting with this build, the Insider Hub app is no longer installed by default but can be reinstalled from the Settings app. The legacy Windows Photo viewer app no longer has various picture format associations in the registry in favor of the Photos app.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://howtogeek.com/225844/how-to-make-windows-photo-viewer-your-default-image-viewer-on-windows-10|title=How to make Windows Photo Viewer your default image viewer in Windows 10|access-date=2020-02-07|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050327/https://www.howtogeek.com/225844/how-to-make-windows-photo-viewer-your-default-image-viewer-on-windows-10/|archive-date=2019-10-31|url-status=live}}</ref>

Microsoft Edge has also received significant improvements in this build. The browser no longer refers to itself as "Project Spartan";instead, it bears the "Edge" name. Updates to the browser include an optional home toolbar button, the ability to import bookmarks from other browsers, dark theme, the ability to drag and drop tabs to another Microsoft Edge window, and auto-fill of forms and password fields. The user can also set what page Microsoft Edge displays upon startup and whether to display top sites and/or aggregated news content upon opening a new tab. Microsoft Edge can now also continue playing audio and video even when the app is minimized.

| style="background:#fdb3ab;"|10.0.10240.16384<br />Version 1507<br /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/kb/3074661|title=Cumulative Security Update for Windows 10: July 15, 2015|accessdate=April 20, 2017}}</ref>
|KB3074661
|'''Fast and slow ring:'''<br />July 15, 2015
|
This is the first [[Released-to-manufacturing|released to manufacturing]] (RTM) build of Windows 10. It was released to device manufacturers to be preloaded on their devices. This is also the build that was sold to retail stores in a USB installation media for customers who would like to purchase the operating system as a standalone retail product.

=== Version 1511 (November Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 November Update''' (also known as '''version 1511''' and codenamed '''"Threshold 2"''') is the first major update to Windows 10 and the second version of the operating system. It carries the build number 10.0.10586.

New features in this version of Windows 10 include:<ref>{{cite web |last1=Geier |first1=Eric |title=What's New in Windows 10 Version 1511 |url=http://techgenix.com/whats-new-windows-10-version-1511/ |website=TechGenix |publisher=TechGenix Ltd. |accessdate=27 March 2019}}</ref>
* Pre-installed [[Skype]] video, messaging, and phone apps
* Tab previews and syncing in Microsoft Edge
* Visual and functional tweaks

The first preview was released on August 18, 2015. The final release was made available to Windows Insiders on November 3, 2015, followed by a public release on November 12, 2015. Unlike the initial release of Windows, this branch was also made available to existing [[Windows Phone 8.1]] devices and the [[Xbox One]] and as a preview release to [[Windows Server 2016]], and was pre-installed on new [[Windows 10 Mobile]] devices. Support of this version for users of the Current Branch (CB) and Current Branch for Business (CBB) ended on October 10, 2017.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/4036927/windows-10-version-1511-end-of-service-for-cb-and-cbb-july-27-2017|title=Windows 10 version 1511 end of service for CB and CBB (July 27, 2017)|date=July 27, 2017|website=Microsoft Support}}</ref> The last public update was released on April 10, 2018, for Enterprise and Education versions only. {{r|ms-win10-release-info}}

|'''Fast ring:'''<br />November 5, 2015<br />'''Slow ring:'''<br />November 9, 2015<br />'''Public release:'''<br />November 12, 2015
|
In this build [[BitLocker]] adds support for [[disk encryption theory#XTS|XTS]]-[[Advanced Encryption Standard|AES]] encryption algorithm.<ref>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 Version 1511 gets new XTS-AES BitLocker encryption algorithm|url=http://winbeta.org/news/windows-10-version-1511-gets-new-xts-aes-bitlocker-encryption-algorithm|website=WinBeta|accessdate=November 13, 2015}}</ref> Other security related features include Enhanced Credential Guard.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://winbeta.org/news/microsoft-enhances-credential-guard-windows-10-november-update|title=Microsoft enhances Credential Guard in Windows 10 November update – WinBeta|website=winbeta.org|accessdate=November 13, 2016}}</ref> In the Settings app, under Privacy, ''Call History'' and ''Email'' are now included.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://winsupersite.com/windows-10/windows-10-november-update-new-privacy-settings|title=Windows 10 November Update: New Privacy Settings|website=SuperSite for Windows|accessdate=January 10, 2016}}</ref> Starting with this build, [[Windows Spotlight]] is available on the [[Windows 10 Pro]] edition.

=== Version 1607 (Anniversary Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 Anniversary Update''' (also known as '''version 1607''' and codenamed '''"Redstone 1"''')<ref>{{cite web|url=http://news.softpedia.com/news/new-windows-10-anniversary-update-build-to-launch-soon-502579.shtml|title=New Windows 10 Anniversary Update Build to Launch "Soon"|work=[[Softpedia]] News|date=April 5, 2016|first=Bogdan|last=Popa|access-date=February 13, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190420131821/https://news.softpedia.com/news/new-windows-10-anniversary-update-build-to-launch-soon-502579.shtml|archive-date=April 20, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://pcworld.com/article/3049362/windows/windows-10-anniversary-update-headed-to-all-users-this-summer.html|title=Windows 10 'Anniversary Update' headed to all users this summer. The next big Windows update adds features for Windows Hello, Cortana, Ink, and more|work=[[PC World]]|date=March 30, 2016|first=Jared|last=Newman|access-date=February 13, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180522181714/https://www.pcworld.com/article/3049362/windows/windows-10-anniversary-update-headed-to-all-users-this-summer.html|archive-date=May 22, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://thurrott.com/windows/windows-10/65762/build-2016-windows-10-redstone-branded-anniversary-update|title=Build 2016: Windows 10 "Redstone" to be Branded as Anniversary Update|work=Thurrott|date=March 30, 2016|first=Paul|last=Thurrott|access-date=February 13, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191031050334/https://www.thurrott.com/windows/windows-10/65762/build-2016-windows-10-redstone-branded-anniversary-update|archive-date=October 31, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="rs2">{{cite web|url=http://winbeta.org/news/windows-10-redstone-rs2-to-launch-in-spring-2017-rs1-coming-this-june|title=Windows 10 Redstone: Second wave of updates coming in 2017|website=WinBeta|accessdate=April 21, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160423095542/http://www.winbeta.org/news/windows-10-redstone-rs2-to-launch-in-spring-2017-rs1-coming-this-june|archive-date=April 23, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref> is the second major update to Windows 10 and the first in a series of updates under the Redstone codenames.{{r|rs2}}<ref>{{cite web|title=Microsoft's 'Redstone': An update to Windows 10 due in 2016|url=http://zdnet.com/article/microsofts-redstone-an-update-to-windows-10-due-in-2016|website=All About Microsoft|accessdate=January 29, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160208114407/http://www.zdnet.com/article/microsofts-redstone-an-update-to-windows-10-due-in-2016/|archive-date=February 8, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://zdnet.com/article/microsoft-pushes-back-windows-10-redstone-2-to-spring-2017-to-line-up-with-new-microsoft-device-wave|title=Microsoft pushes back Windows 10 'Redstone' 2 to Spring 2017 to line up with new Microsoft device wave {{!}} ZDNet|last=Foley|first=Mary Jo|website=ZDNet|accessdate=April 20, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160415191528/http://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-pushes-back-windows-10-redstone-2-to-spring-2017-to-line-up-with-new-microsoft-device-wave/|archive-date=April 15, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref> It carries the build number 10.0.14393. The first preview was released on December 16, 2015. The final release was made available to Windows Insiders on July 18, 2016, followed by a public release on August 2.<ref>{{cite web|last=Bright|first=Peter|url=https://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2016/06/windows-10-anniversary-update-coming-august-2-for-350-million-windows-10-users|title=Windows 10 Anniversary Update coming August 2 for 350 million Windows 10 users|publisher=Ars Technica|date=June 29, 2016|accessdate=July 2, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160702164139/http://arstechnica.com/information-technology/2016/06/windows-10-anniversary-update-coming-august-2-for-350-million-windows-10-users/|archive-date=July 2, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2016/06/29/windows-10-anniversary-update-available-august-2|title=Windows 10 Anniversary Update Available August 2|date=June 29, 2016|accessdate=July 3, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160629140111/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2016/06/29/windows-10-anniversary-update-available-august-2/|archive-date=June 29, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2016/08/02/how-to-get-the-windows-10-anniversary-update|title=How to get the Windows 10 Anniversary Update|date=August 2, 2016|accessdate=August 2, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180714122947/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2016/08/02/how-to-get-the-windows-10-anniversary-update/|archive-date=July 14, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> This release of Windows 10 is supported for users of the Current Branch (CB), Current Branch for Business (CBB) and Long-Term Support Branch (LTSB).

=== Version 1703 (Creators Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 Creators Update'''<ref>{{cite web|url=https://venturebeat.com/2016/10/26/microsoft-unveils-windows-10-creators-update-coming-in-early-2017|title=Microsoft unveils Windows 10 Creators Update, coming in 'early 2017'|last=Protalinski|first=Emil|date=October 26, 2016|website=VentureBeat|publisher=|accessdate=October 26, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161029011605/http://venturebeat.com/2016/10/26/microsoft-unveils-windows-10-creators-update-coming-in-early-2017/|archive-date=October 29, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 1703''' and codenamed '''"Redstone 2"''') is the third major update to Windows 10 and the second in a series of updates under the Redstone codenames.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://windowscentral.com/windows-10-redstone-2-looking-likely-march-2017-release|title=Windows 10 Redstone 2 looking likely for a March 2017 release – Zac Bowden News|date=October 13, 2016|newspaper=Zac Bowden News|accessdate=October 13, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161015072715/http://www.windowscentral.com/windows-10-redstone-2-looking-likely-march-2017-release|archive-date=October 15, 2016|url-status=live}}</ref> It carries the build number 10.0.15063. The first preview was released to Insiders on August 11, 2016. The final release was made available to Windows Insiders on March 20, 2017, followed by a public release on April 5 via Update Assistant, and began to roll out on April 11.<ref>{{cite web|title=Managing the Windows 10 Creators Update rollout for a seamless experience|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2017/03/30/managing-windows-10-creators-update-rollout-seamless-experience|website=Windows Experience Blog|date=March 30, 2017|accessdate=April 15, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170422085504/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2017/03/30/managing-windows-10-creators-update-rollout-seamless-experience/|archive-date=April 22, 2017|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Version 1709 (Fall Creators Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 Fall Creators Update'''<ref>{{cite web|title=Microsoft Announces Windows 10 Fall Creators Update (Redstone 3) Coming in September 2017|first=Vishal|last=Gupta|date=May 11, 2017|url=http://askvg.com/microsoft-announces-redstone-3-coming-in-september-2017|website=AskVG|accessdate=May 12, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170517134805/http://www.askvg.com/microsoft-announces-redstone-3-coming-in-september-2017/|archive-date=May 17, 2017|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 1709''' and codenamed '''"Redstone 3"''') is the fourth major update to Windows 10 and the third in a series of updates under the Redstone codenames. It carries the build number 10.0.16299. The first preview was released to Insiders on April 7, 2017. The final release was made available to Windows Insiders on September 26, 2017 before being released to the public on October 17.<ref>{{cite web|title=What's new in the Windows 10 Fall Creators Update|first=Mollie|last=Ruiz-Hopper|date=October 17, 2017|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2017/10/17/whats-new-windows-10-fall-creators-update|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=October 17, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171017133100/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2017/10/17/whats-new-windows-10-fall-creators-update/|archive-date=October 17, 2017|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Version 1803 (April 2018 Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 April 2018 Update'''<ref>{{cite web|title=Make the most of your time with the new Windows 10 update|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/04/27/make-the-most-of-your-time-with-the-new-windows-10-update|website=Windows Experience Blog|date=April 27, 2018|accessdate=April 27, 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Microsoft's Windows 10 April 2018 Update arrives on Monday|url=https://theverge.com/2018/4/27/17289598/microsoft-windows-10-april-2018-update-release-date-features|website=The Verge|accessdate=April 27, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180427144908/https://www.theverge.com/2018/4/27/17289598/microsoft-windows-10-april-2018-update-release-date-features|archive-date=27 April 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 1803'''<ref name="v1803">{{cite web|title=Windows 10 Redstone 4 is Version 1803 followed by Version 1809, reveals official documentation|url=https://thewincentral.com/windows-10-redstone-4-version-1803-followed-version-1809-reveals-official-documentation|website=WinCentral|publisher=Nayan|date=July 30, 2017|accessdate=August 6, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180726104019/https://thewincentral.com/windows-10-redstone-4-version-1803-followed-version-1809-reveals-official-documentation/|archive-date=July 26, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> and codenamed '''"Redstone 4"''') is the fifth major update to Windows 10 and the fourth in a series of updates under the Redstone codenames. It carries the build number 10.0.17134. The first preview was released to Insiders on August 31, 2017. The final release was made available to Windows Insiders on April 16, 2018, followed by a public release on April 30, and began to roll out on May 8.<ref>{{cite web|title=What's new in the Windows 10 April 2018 Update|first=Mollie|last=Ruiz-Hopper|date=April 30, 2018|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/04/30/whats-new-in-the-windows-10-april-2018-update|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=April 30, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180430175340/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/04/30/whats-new-in-the-windows-10-april-2018-update/|archive-date=30 April 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=How to get the Windows 10 April 2018 Update|first=John|last=Cable|date=April 30, 2018|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/04/30/how-to-get-the-windows-10-april-2018-update|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=May 1, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180501014830/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/04/30/how-to-get-the-windows-10-april-2018-update/|archive-date=1 May 2018|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Version 1809 (October 2018 Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 October 2018 Update'''<ref>{{cite web|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/08/31/showcasing-new-computing-possibilities-at-ifa|title=Showcasing new computing possibilities at IFA|website=Windows Experience Blog|language=en-US|access-date=2018-08-31|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180901044603/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/08/31/showcasing-new-computing-possibilities-at-ifa/|archive-date=2018-09-01|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 1809'''{{r|v1803}} and codenamed '''"Redstone 5"''') is the sixth major update to Windows 10 and the fifth in a series of updates under the Redstone codenames. It carries the build number 10.0.17763. The first preview was released to Insiders on February 14, 2018. The update was originally made available to public consumers on October 2, 2018,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/10/02/find-out-whats-new-in-windows-and-office-in-october|title=Find out what's new in Windows and Office in October|accessdate=2018-10-02|website=Windows Experience Blog}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/10/02/how-to-get-the-windows-10-october-2018-update|title=How to get the Windows 10 October 2018 Update|accessdate=2018-10-02|website=Windows Experience Blog|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181002222658/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/10/02/how-to-get-the-windows-10-october-2018-update/|archive-date=2 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> but its rollout was halted on October 6, 2018, due to a serious bug that deletes users' personal files after updating.<ref>{{cite web|title=windows 10 (October 2018 update) (version 1809) deleted all my files|url=https://answers.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/forum/windows_10-files/windows-10-october-2018-update-version-1809/1a924008-ddba-48db-a96f-7b4bfef9039a|website=Microsoft Community|accessdate=October 7, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181007053109/https://answers.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/forum/windows_10-files/windows-10-october-2018-update-version-1809/1a924008-ddba-48db-a96f-7b4bfef9039a|archive-date=October 7, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 October update is no longer being provided by any of the methods|url=https://answers.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/forum/all/windows-10-october-update-is-no-longer-being/62e8e6b4-0089-41c2-a104-5a5a768a48f6|website=Microsoft Community|accessdate=October 7, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181010011035/https://answers.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/forum/all/windows-10-october-update-is-no-longer-being/62e8e6b4-0089-41c2-a104-5a5a768a48f6|archive-date=October 10, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Microsoft pulls Windows 10 October Update (version 1809)|url=https://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-pulls-windows-10-october-update-version-1809|first=Catalin|last=Cimpanu|website=[[ZDNet]]|date=October 6, 2018|accessdate=October 7, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181007053109/https://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-pulls-windows-10-october-update-version-1809/|archive-date=October 7, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> On October 9, 2018, Microsoft re-released the update to Insiders, stating that all known issues in the update (including file deletion bug) had been identified and fixed.<ref name="b17763update">{{cite web|title=Updated version of Windows 10 October 2018 Update released to Windows Insiders|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/10/09/updated-version-of-windows-10-october-2018-update-released-to-windows-insiders|website=Windows Experience Blog|first=John|last=Cable|date=October 9, 2018|accessdate=October 9, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181009213206/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/10/09/updated-version-of-windows-10-october-2018-update-released-to-windows-insiders/|archive-date=9 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Windows 10 October 2018 Update rereleased to Insiders, data loss blamed on misdirected folders|url=https://www.pcworld.com/article/3312642/windows/microsoft-restarts-windows-10-october-2018-update-blaming-data-loss-on-misdirected-folders.html|first=Mark|last=Hachman|website=[[PC World]]|date=October 9, 2018|accessdate=October 9, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181010070253/https://www.pcworld.com/article/3312642/windows/microsoft-restarts-windows-10-october-2018-update-blaming-data-loss-on-misdirected-folders.html|archive-date=10 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> On October 25, 2018, Microsoft confirmed the existence of another bug which overwrites files without any confirmation, when extracting from a [[Zip (file format)|ZIP file]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Microsoft confirms ZIP bug in Windows 10 October 2018 Update|url=https://www.techradar.com/news/microsoft-confirms-zip-bug-in-windows-10-october-2018-update-and-offers-advice|website=TechRadar|accessdate=October 25, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181025125610/https://www.techradar.com/news/microsoft-confirms-zip-bug-in-windows-10-october-2018-update-and-offers-advice|archive-date=25 October 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> The ZIP bug was fixed for Insiders on October 30, 2018,<ref name="b17763.107">{{cite news|title=Microsoft releases Windows 10 build 17763.107 to Insiders to fix the October 2018 Update|url=https://www.neowin.net/news/microsoft-releases-windows-10-build-17763107-to-insiders-to-fix-the-october-2018-update|first=Rich|last=Woods|website=[[Neowin]]|date=October 30, 2018|accessdate=October 30, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181030190359/https://www.neowin.net/news/microsoft-releases-windows-10-build-17763107-to-insiders-to-fix-the-october-2018-update|archive-date=October 30, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> and the public rollout of the update resumed on November 13, 2018.<ref>{{cite web|title=Resuming the rollout of the Windows 10 October 2018 Updates|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/11/13/resuming-the-rollout-of-the-windows-10-october-2018-update|website=Windows Experience Blog|first=John|last=Cable|date=November 13, 2018|accessdate=November 14, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181114000224/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2018/11/13/resuming-the-rollout-of-the-windows-10-october-2018-update/|archive-date=14 November 2018|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Microsoft resumes rollout of Windows 10 version 1809, promises quality changes|url=https://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-resumes-rollout-of-windows-10-version-1809-promises-quality-changes|first=Ed|last=Bott|website=[[ZDNet]]|date=November 13, 2018|accessdate=November 14, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181113210132/https://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-resumes-rollout-of-windows-10-version-1809-promises-quality-changes/|archive-date=November 13, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Version 1903 (May 2019 Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 May 2019 Update'''<ref>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 May 2019 Update gets official, late-May planned release|first=Zac|last=Bowden|date=April 4, 2019|url=https://www.windowscentral.com/microsoft-announces-windows-10-may-2019-update|website=Windows Central|accessdate=April 4, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190404174718/https://www.windowscentral.com/microsoft-announces-windows-10-may-2019-update|archive-date=4 April 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 1903'''<ref>{{cite web|title=Windows 10 version 1809 & 1903 to follow version 1803 (Redstone 4), confirms official slides|url=https://thewincentral.com/windows-10-version-1809-1903-follow-version-1803-redstone-4-confirms-official-slides|website=WinCentral|accessdate=July 25, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180726232410/https://thewincentral.com/windows-10-version-1809-1903-follow-version-1803-redstone-4-confirms-official-slides/|archive-date=July 26, 2018|url-status=live}}</ref> and codenamed '''"19H1"'''{{r|b17723&18204}}) is the seventh major update to Windows 10 and the first to use a more descriptive codename (including the year and the order released) instead of the "Redstone"<ref>{{cite news|url=https://windowscentral.com/microsoft-move-away-windows-10-redstone-codenames|title=Microsoft to move away from 'Redstone' codename for Windows 10 updates in 2019|date=2018-03-28|work=Windows Central|access-date=2018-07-29|language=en|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180731062219/https://www.windowscentral.com/microsoft-move-away-windows-10-redstone-codenames|archive-date=2018-07-31|url-status=live}}</ref> or "Threshold" codename. It carries the build number 10.0.18362. The first preview was released to Insiders who opted in to the exclusive Skip Ahead ring on July 25, 2018. The update began rolling out on May 21, 2019.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/microsoft/microsoft-releases-windows-10-version-1903-may-2019-update/|title=Microsoft Releases Windows 10 Version 1903 - May 2019 Update|website=BleepingComputer|language=en-us|access-date=2019-05-21|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190522204734/https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/microsoft/microsoft-releases-windows-10-version-1903-may-2019-update/|archive-date=2019-05-22|url-status=live}}</ref>
Notable changes in the May 2019 Update include:<ref>{{Cite web|title=Windows 10 May 2019 Update review: Simple changes make Microsoft's OS run smoother|first=Zac|last=Bowden|url=https://www.windowscentral.com/windows-10-may-2019-update-review|website=Windows Central|publisher=Mobile Nations|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200301023233/https://www.windowscentral.com/windows-10-may-2019-update-review|archive-date=1 March 2020|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=The top ten Windows 10 May 2019 Update features|first=Mary|last=Branscombe|url=https://www.techrepublic.com/article/the-top-ten-windows-10-may-2019-update-features/|website=TechRepublic|publisher=CBS Interactive|access-date=5 March 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190703195934/https://www.techrepublic.com/article/the-top-ten-windows-10-may-2019-update-features/|archive-date=3 July 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>
* A new "light theme"
* Separation of Search and Cortana in the taskbar
* Windows Sandbox (not available in Windows 10 Home)
* Ability to pause updates for 35 days or under (incl. Windows 10 Home)
* New default wallpaper
* Recommended troubleshooting
* Notifications hidden while in full-screen

=== Version 1909 (November 2019 Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 November 2019 Update'''<ref name="nov2019update">{{cite web|title=Getting the November 2019 Update Ready for Release|first=Brandon|last=LeBlanc|date=October 10, 2019|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/10/10/getting-the-november-2019-update-ready-for-release/|website=Windows Insider Blog|accessdate=October 11, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191011073422/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/10/10/getting-the-november-2019-update-ready-for-release/|archive-date=October 11, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 1909'''{{r|19H1H2CU}} and codenamed '''"19H2"''') is the eighth major update to Windows 10.<ref name="19H2&20H1">{{cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 18836|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/02/14/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-18836|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=February 16, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190216061302/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/02/14/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-18836/|archive-date=February 16, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> The update is delivered as cumulative update to the May 2019 Update and carries the build number 10.0.18363. The first preview was released to Insiders who opted in to the slow ring on July 1, 2019.<ref name="b10000">{{cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 18362.10000 (19H2)|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/07/01/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-18362-10000-19h2|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=July 1, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190702005741/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/07/01/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-18362-10000-19h2/|archive-date=July 2, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> The update began rolling out on November 12, 2019.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Microsoft begins the official rollout of Windows 10 1909|first=Mary|last=Jo Foley|url=https://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-begins-the-official-rollout-of-windows-10-1909/|website=ZDNet|access-date=November 12, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191113012311/https://www.zdnet.com/article/microsoft-begins-the-official-rollout-of-windows-10-1909/|archive-date=November 13, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> Notable changes in the November 2019 Update include:<ref>{{Cite web|title=How to get the Windows 10 November 2019 Update|date=2019-11-12|website=Windows Experience Blog|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/11/12/how-to-get-the-windows-10-november-2019-update|access-date=November 13, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191113013709/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/11/12/how-to-get-the-windows-10-november-2019-update/|archive-date=13 November 2019|url-status=live}}</ref>

* Ability to create events from the Calendar fly-out on the taskbar
* Improvements to notification management, including thumbnails demonstrating notification banners and the Action Center in application notification settings, and the ability to access per-application notification settings from their displays in Action Center
* The Start menu's navigation sidebar icons expand into a drawer with text labels when the cursor is hovered over them
* Support for using third-party digital assistants from the lock screen
* OneDrive integration with File Explorer's search

|'''Slow ring:'''<br />July 1, 2019

=== Version 2004 (May 2020 Update) ===
The '''Windows 10 May 2020 Update'''<ref name="may2020update">{{cite web|title=Getting the May 2020 Update Ready for Release|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/04/16/getting-the-may-2020-update-ready-for-release|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=April 16, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200417044205/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/04/16/getting-the-may-2020-update-ready-for-release/|archive-date=April 17, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> (also known as '''version 2004'''<ref name="b19033">{{Cite web|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/11/26/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19033/|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 19033|website=Windows Experience Blog|access-date=November 27, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191127184021/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/11/26/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19033/|archive-date=November 27, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> and codenamed '''"20H1"''') is the ninth major update to Windows 10. It carries the build number 10.0.19041. The first preview was released to Insiders who opted in to the exclusive Skip Ahead ring on February 14, 2019.{{r|19H2&20H1}} The update began rolling out on May 27, 2020.<ref name="20H1">{{cite web|title=How to get the Windows 10 May 2020 Update|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/05/27/how-to-get-the-windows-10-may-2020-update|website=Windows Blog|date=May 27, 2020|accessdate=May 27, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200527201549/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/05/27/how-to-get-the-windows-10-may-2020-update/|archive-date=27 May 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>
Notable changes in the May 2020 Update include:<ref>{{cite web|title=What's New in the Windows 10 May 2020 Update|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/05/27/whats-new-in-the-windows-10-may-2020-update|website=Windows Blog|date=May 27, 2020|accessdate=May 27, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200528052847/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/05/27/whats-new-in-the-windows-10-may-2020-update/|archive-date=28 May 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>
* Faster and easier access to Bluetooth settings and pairing
* Improved Kaomojis
* Virtual Desktops are now renamable 
* [[DirectX#DirectX 12 Ultimate|DirectX 12 Ultimate]]
* Introducing a chat-based UI for Cortana
* Greater integration with [[Android (operating system)|Android]] smartphones on the Your Phone app
* Windows Subsystem for Linux 2
* Ability to use Windows Hello without the need for a password
* Ability to use Windows Hello PIN while in [[Safe mode]]
* Cloud download option to reset Windows
* Accessibility improvements

=== Version 20H2 ===
The tenth major update to Windows 10 (codenamed '''"20H2"'''<ref>{{cite web|title=What’s next for Windows 10 updates|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/16/whats-next-for-windows-10-updates/|website=Windows Blog|date=June 16, 2020|accessdate=June 18, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200617150742/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/16/whats-next-for-windows-10-updates/|archive-date=June 17, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>) is delivered as cumulative update to the May 2020 Update, and carries the build number 10.0.19042. The first preview was released to Insiders who opted in to Beta Channel on June 16, 2020.<ref name=b19042-330>{{cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 19042.330 (20H2)|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/16/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19042-330-20h2|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=June 18, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200617143944/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/16/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19042-330-20h2/|archive-date=June 17, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Dev Channel (Fast Ring) ===

On December 16, 2019, Microsoft announced that Windows Insiders in the Fast Ring will receive builds directly from the "RS_PRERELEASE" development branch. Builds released from the Fast Ring are no longer matched to a specific Windows 10 release. The first build released under the new strategy, build 19536, was made available to Insiders on the same day.<ref name="fastring">{{cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 19536|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/12/16/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19536|accessdate=January 14, 2020|website=Windows Experience Blog|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200113223817/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2019/12/16/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19536/|archive-date=January 13, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

On May 13, 2020, Microsoft announced that builds from the "MN_RELEASE" branch would be available to Windows Insiders in the Fast Ring for a short period of time.<ref name="b19628">{{Cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 19628|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/05/13/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19628|access-date=May 14, 2020|website=Windows Experience Blog|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200517050448/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/05/13/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-19628/|archive-date=May 17, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref>

As of June 15, 2020, Microsoft has introduced "channels" model to its Windows Insider Program, succeeding its "ring" model.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Introducing Windows Insider Channels|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/15/introducing-windows-insider-channels|website=Windows Experience Blog|first=Amanda|last=Langowski|date=June 15, 2020|accessdate=June 16, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200616060138/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/15/introducing-windows-insider-channels/|archive-date=June 16, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Therefore, all future builds (starting from build 10.0.20150) would be released to Windows Insiders in the Dev Channel.<ref name="b20150">{{cite web|title=Announcing Windows 10 Insider Preview Build 20150|url=https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/17/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-20150|website=Windows Experience Blog|accessdate=June 18, 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200617234157/https://blogs.windows.com/windowsexperience/2020/06/17/announcing-windows-10-insider-preview-build-20150/|archive-date=June 17, 2020|url-status=live}}</ref> Two days later (June 17), Microsoft announced that Windows Insiders in the Dev Channel would be once again received builds from "RS_PRERELEASE" development branch.{{r|b20150}}
